It may be that, in a given case, the material information may be such that the Union of India may feel it necessary to claim the privilege provided by Section.	None
123 of the Indian Evidence Act.	None
As and when such claim is made, it is obvious, it will be dealt with according to law.	None
While on this question, we may mention that if in a given case the proclamation contains the reasons, with adequate specificity, for which the proclamation was issued, the Court may have to be satisfied before calling upon the Union of India to produce the. material information that the reasons given in the proclamation are prima facie irrelevant to the formation of the requisite satisfaction and or that it is a fit case where the Union of India must yet be called upon to place the material information on the basis of which it had formed the satisfaction.	None
The Union of India may perhaps be well advised to follow the practice of stating the reasons and the grounds upon which the requisite satisfaction is founded.	None
Article 356  Is it confined only to cases where the State Government fails or refuses to abide by the directions issued by the Central Government?	None
It was submitted by Sri Jethamalani, the learned counsel for some of the petitioners that in view of Article 365 of the Constitution, the only situation in which the power under Article 356 can be invoked by the President is the failure of the State Government to comply with or to give effect to the directions given in exercise of the executive power of the Union under any of the provisions of the Constitution and not in any other case.	Arguments of Petitioner
Reference is made in this connection to Articles 256 and 257.	None
It would be appropriate to read all the three Articles at this stage Obligation of States and the Union  The executive power of every State shall be so exercised as to ensure compliance with the laws made by Parliament and any existing laws which apply in that State and the executive power of the Union shall extend to the giving of such directions to a State as may appear to the Government of India to be necessary for that purpose.	None
Control of the Union over States in certain cases  (1) The executive power of every State shall be so exercised as not to impede or prejudice the exercise of the executive power of the Union, and the executive power of the Union shall extend to the giving of such directions to a State as may appear to the Government of India to be necessary for that purposes.	None
The executive power of the Union shall also extend to the giving of directions to a State as to the construction and maintenance of means of communication, declared in the direction to be of national or military importance Provided that nothing in this clause shall be taken as restricting the power of Parliament to declare highways or waterways to be national highways or national waterways or the power of the Union with respect to the highways or waterways so declared or the power of the Union to construct and maintain means of communication as part of its functions with respect to naval, military and air force works.	None
The executive power of the Union shall also extend to the giving of directions to a State as to the measures to be taken for the protection of the railways within the State.	None
Wherein carrying out any direction given to a State under clause (2) as to the construction or maintenance of any means of communication or under clause (3) as to the measures to be taken for protection of any railway, costs have been incurred in excess of those which would have been incurred in the discharge of the normal duties of the State if such direction had not been given, there shall be paid by the Government of India to the State such sum as may be agreed, or, in default of agreement, as may be determined by an arbitrator appointed by the Chief Justice of India in respect of the extra costs so incurred by the State.	None
Effect of failure to comply with, or to give effect to, directions given by the Union Where any State has failed to comply with, or to give effect to, any directions given in the exercise of the executive power of the union under any of the provisions of this Constitution, it shall be lawful for the President to hold that a situation has arisen in which the government of the State cannot be carried on in accordance with the provisions of this Constitution.	None
In our opinion, the contention urged is unacceptable.	None
Article 256 merely states that the executive power of every State shall be so exercised as to ensure compliance with the laws made by the Parliament whether existing or to be made in future.	None
It is stated therein that the executive power of the Union shall extend to giving of such directions to a State as may appear to the Government of India to be necessary for the said purpose.	None
This Article is confined to proper and due implemention of the parliamentary enactments and the power to give directions for that purpose.	None
Article 257 says that executive power of every State shall be so exercised as not to impede or prejudice the exercise of the executive power of the Union for ensuring the same, the Union Government is empowered to give appropriate directions.	None
Clauses (2), (3) and (4) illustrate and elaborate the power contained in clause (1).	None
Article 365, which incidentally does not occur in Part XVIII, but in Part XIX ( Miscellaneous) merely says that where any State has failed to comply with or give effect to any directions given by the Union of India in exercise of its executive power under any of the provisions of the Constitution, it shall be lawful for the President to hold that a situation has arisen in which the Government of the State cannot be carried on in accordance with the provisions of the Constitution.	None
The article merely sets out one instance in which the President may hold that the Government of the State cannot be carried on in accordance with the provisions of the Constitution.	None
It cannot be read as exhaustive of the situation where the President may form the said satisfaction.	None
Suffice it to say that the directions given must be lawful and their disobdience must give rise to a situation contemplated by Art.	None
356(l).	None
Article 365 merely says that in case of failure to comply with the directions given, it shall be lawful for the President to hold that the requisite type of situation (contemplated by Article 356(1)) has arisen.	None
It is not as if each and every failure ipso facto gives rise to the requisite situation.	None
The President has to judge in each case whether it has not arisen.	None
Article 365 says it is permissible for him to say so in such a case.	None
The discretion is still there and has to be exercised fairly.	None
Facts and Merits of Individual cases Karnataka By a proclamation dated April 21, 1989 the President dismissed the Government of Karnataka, dissolved the Legislative Assembly, took over the powers of the government and the Governor, vested the powers of the State legislature in the Parliament and made other incidental and ancillary provisions suspending several provisions of the Constitution with respect to that State.	Facts
The proclamation does not contain any reasons except barely reciting the satisfaction of the President.	Facts
The satisfaction is stated to have been formed on a consideration of the report of the Governor and other information received by him.	Facts
Sri S. R. Bommai was the Chief Minister then.	Facts
The Janata Legislature party emerged as the majority party in the State Legislature following elections to the Assembly in March, 1985.	Facts
Sri Ramakrishna Hedge was elected the leader of the Janata Legislature Party and was sworn in as the Chief Minister in March, 1985.	Facts
In August, 1988, Sri Hegde resigned and Sri Bommai was elected as the leader and sworn in as the Chief Minister on August 30, 1988.	Facts
In September, 1988, Janata Party and Lok Dal(B) merged resulting in the formation of Janata Dal.	Facts
The Janata Party in Karnataka Legislature was renamed Janata Dal.	Facts
On April 15, 1989 the Ministry was expanded by Sri Bommai including thirteen more members.	Facts
On April 17, 1989, a legislator Sri Kalyan Rao Molakery, defected from the party and presented a letter to the Governor withdrawing his support to the Janata Dal Government.	Facts
On the next day, he met the Governor and presented nineteen letters purported to have been signed by seventeen Janata Dal legislators, one associate independent legislator and one B.J.P. legislator withdrawing their support to the Government.	Facts
The Governor is said to have called the Secretary of the Legislature Department and got the authenticity of the signatures on the letters verified.	Facts
He did not, of course, inform Sri Bommai about these developments.	Facts
On April 19, 1989, the Governor sent a report to the President stating that there were dissensions in Janata Party which led to the resignation of Sri Hegde earlier and that even after the formation of Janata Dal, there have been dissensions and defections.	Facts
He referred to the letters received by him from defecting members and opined that on that account, the ruling party has been reduced to minority in the Assembly.	Facts
He stated that the council of ministers headed by Sri Bommai does not command a majority in the House and that, therefore, it is not appropriate under the Constitution to have the State administered by an executive consisting of council of ministers who do not command the majority in the House.	Facts
He opined that no. other party is in a position to form the Government and, recommended action under Article 356(l).	Facts
On April 20, 1989, seven legislators out of those who were said to have submitted the letters to the Governor complaining that their signatures were obtained on those letters by misrepresentation and by misleading them.	Facts
They reaffirmed their support to the Bommai Ministry.	Facts
On the same day, the State Cabinet met and decided to convene the Assembly session on April 27, 1989.	Facts
The Chief Minister and the Law Minister met the Governor on that day itself and informed him about the summoning of the Assembly session.	Facts
They also brought to the Governors notice the recommendation of the Sarkaria Commission that the support and strength of the Chief Minister should be tested on the floor of the Assembly.	Facts
Sri Bommai offered to prove his majority on the floor of the House.	Facts
He even expressed his readiness to prepone the Assembly Session if so desired by the Governor.	Facts
He also sent a telex message to that effect to the President of India.	Facts
In spite of all this, the Governor sent another report to the President of India on April 20, 1989 referring to the letter of seven members withdrawing their earlier letters and opining that the said letters were evidently obtained by Sri Bommai by pressuring those M.L.As.	Facts
He reported that horsetrading is going on and atmosphere is getting vitiated.	Facts
He reiterated his opinion that Sri Bommai has lost the confidence of the majority in the State Assembly and requested action being taken on his previous letter.	Facts
On that very day, the President issued the proclamation.	Facts
It says that the said action was taken on the basis of the report from the Governor of the State of Karnataka and other information received.	Facts
Both the Houses of Parliament duly met and approved the said proclamation as contemplated by clause (3) of Article 356.	Facts
The validity of the proclamation was challenged by Sri Bommai and certain other members of the council of ministers by way of a writ petition (W.P. 7899 of 1989) in the Karnataka High Court.	Facts
The Union of India (the first respondent in the writ petition) submitted that the decision of the President of India based on the report of the Governor and other information brought to his notice is not justiciable and cannot be challenged in the writ petition.	Facts
While making a report, it was submitted, the Governor does not act on the aid and advice of his council of ministers but in his individual capacity.	Facts
The report of the Governor cannot be challenged in view of Article 361 of the Constitution nor can he or the President be compelled to disclose the information or material upon which they have acted.	Facts
Article 74(2) was said to be a bar to the Court enquiring into the said information, material and advice.	Facts
It was also submitted that the proclamation has since been approved by both Houses of Parliament under clause (3) of Article 356.	Facts
The State of Karnataka submitted that the Governor had taken into consideration all the facts and circumstances prevailing in the State while submitting his report and that the proclamation issued on that basis is unobjectionable.	Facts
A Special Bench of threeJudges of High Court heard the writ petition and dismissed the same on the following reasoning The proclamation under Article 356(l) is not immune from judicial scrutiny.	Facts
The court can examine whether the satisfaction has been formed on wholly extraneous material or whether there is a rational nexus between the material and the satisfaction.	Facts
In Article 356 the President means the Union council of ministers.	Facts
The satisfaction referred to therein is subjective satisfaction.	Facts
This satisfaction has no. doubt to be formed on a consideration of all the facts and circumstances.	Facts
The two reports of the Governor conveyed to the President essential and relevant facts which were relevant for the purpose of Article 356.	Facts
The facts stated in the Governors report cannot be stated to be irrelevant.	Facts
They are perfectly relevant.	None
Where the Governors personal bona fides are not questioned, his satisfaction that no. other party is in a position to form the government has to be accepted as true and is based upon a reasonable assessment of all the relevant facts.	None
Recourse to floor test was neither compulsory nor obligatory.	Facts
It was not a prerequisite to sending up a report recommending action under Article 356(l).	Facts
The introduction of Xth Schedule to the Constitution has not affected in any manner the content of the power under Article 356.	None
Since the proclamation has to be issued on the satisfaction of the Union council of ministers the Governors report cannot be faulted on the ground of legal mala fides.	Facts
Applying the test indicated in the State of Rajasthan v. Union of India, the court must hold, on the basis of material disclosed, that the subjective satisfaction arrived at by the President is conclusive and cannot be faulted.	Facts
The proclamation, therefore, is unobjectionable.	Facts
We find ourselves unable to agree with the High Court except on points (1) and (2).	None
To begin with, we must say that question of personal bona fides of Governor is really irrelevant.	Reasoning
We must also say that the observation under point (7) is equally misplaced.	None
It is true that action under Article 356 is taken on the basis of satisfaction of the union Council of Ministers but on that score it cannot be said that legal mala fides of the Governor is irrelevant.	None
When the Article speaks of the satisfaction being formed on the basis of the Governors report, the legal mala fides, if any, of the Governor cannot be said to be irrelevant.	None
The Governors report may not be conclusive but its relevance is undeniable.	None
Action under Article 356 can be based only and exclusively upon such report.	None
Governor is a very high constitutional functionary.	None
He is supposed to act fairly and honestly consistent with his oath.	None
He is actually reporting against his own government.	None
It is for this reason that Article 356 places such implicit faith in his report.	None
If, however, in a given case his report is vitiated by legal mala fides, it is bound to vitiate the Presidents action as well.	None
Regarding the other points made in the judgment of the High Court, we must say that the High Court went wrong in law in approving and upholding the Governors report and the action of the President under Article 356.	None
The Governors report is vitiated by more than one assumption totally unsustainable in law.	None
The Constitution does not create an obligation that the political party forming the ministry should necessarily have a majority in the Legislature.	None
Minority governments are not unknown.	None
What is necessary is that that government should enjoy the confidence of the House.	None
This aspect does not appear to have been kept in mind by the Governor.	None
Secondly and more importantly whether the council of ministers have lost the confidence of the House is not a matter to be determined by the Governor or for that matter anywhere else except the floor of the House.	None
The principle of democracy underlying our Constitution necessarily means that any such question should be decided on the floor of the House.	None
The House is the place where the democracy is in action.	None
It is not for the Governor to determine the said question on his own or on his own Verification.	None
This is not a matter within his subjective satisfaction.	None
It is an objective fact capable of being established on the floor of the House.	None
It is gratifying to note that Sri R. Venkataraman, the former President of India has affirmed this view in his Rajaji Memorial Lecture (Hindustan Times dated February 24, 1994).	None
Exceptional and rare situations may arise where because of all pervading atmosphere of violence or other extraordinary reasons, it may not be possible for the members of the Assembly to express their opinion freely.	None
But no.	None
such situation had arisen here.	None
No. one suggested that any such violent atmosphere was obtaining at the relevant time.	None
In this connection, it would be appropriate to notice the unanimous report of the committee of Governor appointed by the President of India.	None
The five Governors unanimously recommended that the test of confidence in the ministry should normally be left to a vote in the AssemblyWhere the Governor is satisfied by whatever process or means, that the ministry no.	None
longer enjoys majority support, he should ask the Chief Minister to face the Assembly and prove his majority within the shortest possible time.	None
If the Chief Minister shirks this primary responsibility and falls to comply, the Governor would be in duty bound to initiate steps to form an alternative ministry.	None
A Chief Ministers refusal to test his strength on the floor of the Assembly can well be interpreted as prima facie proof of his no. longer enjoying the confidence of the legislature.	None
If then, an alternative ministry can be formed, which, in the Governors view, is able to command a majority in the assembly, he must dismiss the ministry in power and instal the alternative ministry in office.	None
On the other hand, if no.	None
such ministry is possible, the Governor will be left with no. alternative but to make a report to the President under Article 356	None
As a general proposition, it may be stated that, as far as possible, the verdict as to majority support claimed by a Chief Minister and his Council of Ministers should be left to the legislature, and that it is only if a responsible government cannot be maintained without doing violence to correct constitutional practice that the Governor should resort to Article 356 of the Constitution what is important to remember is that recourse to article 356 should be the last resort for a Governor to seekthe guiding principle being, as already stated, that the constitutional machinery in the state should, as far as possible, be maintained.	None
(quoted from the Book Presidents Rule in the States, edited by Sri Rajiv Dhavan and published under the auspices of the Indian Law Institute, New Delhi).	None
It is a pity that the Governor of Karnataka did not keep the above salutary guidelines and principles in mind while making his report.	None
Dr. G.S. Dhillon Speaker, Lok Sabha (in his address to the conference of the Presiding Officers of legislative bodies in India) too affirmed in clear words that whether the ministry continued to command majority support in the legislature, the doubt should as far as possible be left to be resolved on the floor of the House and the Governor should not take upon himself unenviable task of deciding the question himself outside the legislature.	None
The High Court, in our opinion, erred in holding that the floor test is not obligatory.	None
If only one keeps in mind the democractic principle underlying the Constitution and the fact that it is the legislative assembly that represents the will of the people  and not the Governor  the position would be clear beyond any doubt.	None
In this case, it may be remembered that the council of ministers not only decided on April 20, 1989 to convene the Assembly on 27th of that very month i.e., within seven days, but also offered to prepone the Assembly if the Governor so desired.	None
It pains us to note that the Governor did not choose to act upon the said offer.	None
Indeed, it was his duty to summon the Assembly and call upon the Chief Minister to establish that he enjoyed the confidence of the House.	None
Not only did he not do it	None
but when the Council of Ministers offered to do the same, he demurred and chose instead to submit the report to the President.	None
In the circumstances, it cannot be said that the Governors report contained, or was based upon, relevant material.	None
There could be no. question of the Governor making an assessment of his own.	None
The loss of confidence of the House was an objective fact, which could have been demonstrated, one way or the other, on the floor of the House.	None
In our opinion, wherever a doubt arises whether the Council of Ministers has lost the confidence of the House, the only way of testing it is on the floor of the House except in an extraordinary situation where because of all pervasive violence, the Governor comes to the conclusion and records the same in his report that for the reasons Mentioned by him a free vote is not possible in the House.	None
We make it clear that what we have said above is confined to a situation where the incumbent Chief Minister is alleged to have lost the majority support or the confidence of the House.	None
It is not relevant to a situation arising after a generel election where the Governor has to invite the leader of the party commanding majority in the House or the single largest party group to form the government.	None
We need express no. opinion regarding such a situation.	None
We are equally of the opinion that the High Court was in error in holding that enactment addition of Xth Schedule to the Constitution has not made any difference.	None
The very object of the Xth Schedule is to prevent and discourage floorcrossing and defections, which at one time had assumed alarming proportions.	None
Whatever may be his personal predilictions, a legislator elected on the ticket of a party is bound to support that party in case of a division or vote of confidence in the House, unless he is prepared to forgo his membership of the House.	None
The Xth Schedule was designed precisely to counteract horsetrading.	None
Except in the case of a split, a legislator has to support his party willynilly.	None
This is the difference between the position obtaining prior to and after the Xth Schedule.	None
Prior to the said Amendment, a legislator could shift his loyalty from one party to the other any number of times without imperilling his membership of the House  it was as if he had a property in the office.	None
Though the proclamation recites that the Presidents satisfaction was based also on other information received, the counteraffidavit of the Union of India does not indicate or state that any other information material was available to the President or the Union Council of Ministers other than the report of the Governor much less disclose it.	None
In the circumstances, we must hold that there was no.	None
other information before the President except the report of the Governor and that the Word and other information received by me were put in the proclamation mechanically.	None
The Governors report and the facts stated therein appear to be the only basis of dismissing the government and dissolving the Assembly under Article 356(l).	None
The proclamation must, therefore, be held to be not warranted by Article 356.	None
It is outside its purview.	None
It cannot be said, in the circumstances, that the President (or the Union Council of Ministers) was satisfied that the government of the State cannot be carried on in accordance with the provisions of the Constitution.	None
The action was mala fide and unconstitutional.	None
The proclamation is accordingly liable to be struck down and we would have struck it down herewith but for the fact that the elections have since been held to the Legislative Assembly of the State and a new House has come into being.	None
The issuance of a writ at this juncture would be a futile one.	None
But for the said fact, we could certainly have considered restoring the dismissed government to office and reactivating the dissolved Assembly.	None
In any event, the judgment of Karnataka High Court is set aside.	None
MEGHALAYA (TRANSFERRED CASES NOS.	Facts
5 AND 7 OF 1992)	None
In March, 1990, Hill Peoples Union, to which the petitioner, Gonald Stone Massar, belonged and several other State political parties and certain independent M.L.As.	None
joined together to form a front, known as Meghalaya United Parliamentary Party (MUPP).	None
This Front had a majority in the Assembly and formed the government headed by Sri B. B. Lyngdon.	Facts
On July 25, 1991, the then Speaker of the House, Sri P. R. Kyndiah Arthree was elected as the leader of the opposition group known as United Meghalaya Parliamentary Forum (UMPF), which was led by the Congress Party to which Sri Kyndiah belonged.	Facts
He claimed the support of the majority of members in the House and requested the Governor to invite him to form the Government.	Facts
Thereupon the Governor requested Sri Lyngdon to prove his majority on the floor of the House.	Facts
On August 7, 1991, a special session of the Assembly was convened to pass a motion of confidence in the ministry.	Facts
On the motion being moved thirty members supported it and twenty seven voted against it.	Facts
Before announcing the result, however, the Speaker announced that he had received a complaint against five independent M.L.As.	Facts
in the ruling coalition alleging disqualification under the Antidefection Law and that he was forthwith suspending their right to vote.	Facts
This resulted in an uproar in the Assembly.	Facts
The session had to be adjourned.	Facts
On August 11, 1991, the Speaker sent identical showcause notices to the said five independent MLAs on the basis of the complaint filed by one Sri H. S. Shylla.	Facts
On August 16, the five MLAs sent their replies denying that they have joined any of the parties as alleged.	Facts
They affirmed that they continue to remain independents.	Facts
On August 17, 1991 the Speaker passed an order disqualifying all the five MLAs on the basis that four of them were Ministers in the Lyngdon Ministry and one of them (Sri Chamberlain Marak) was the Deputy Government Chief Whip.	Facts
The disqualification, it may be noted, was not on the ground alleged in the show cause notice.	Facts
Meanwhile, on the Governors advice, the Chief Minister summoned the session of the Assembly for September 9, 1991 for passing a vote of confidence.	Facts
The Speaker refused to send the notices of the session to the five MLAs disqualified by him.	Facts
He also made arrangements to ensure that the said five members are not allowed to enter the Assembly.	Facts
On September 6, 1991, four of the said five MLAs approached this court and obtained an interim order staying the operation of the orders of the Speaker dated August 7, 1991 and August 17, 1991.	Facts
(One Member.	Facts
Sri Ch. Marak, did not obtain any such orders).	Facts
On coming to know of the order of this Court, the Speaker issued a press statement saying that he does not accept any, interference by any court with his order dated August 7, 1991 disqualifying five members.	Facts
He issued strict instructions to the security guards not to allow the said five members to enter the Assembly premises.	Facts
In this explosive situation, the Governor adjourned the Assembly indefinitely by an order dated September 8, 1991, After a brief interval and on the advice of the Governor the Assembly Was again summoned to Meet on October 8, 1991.	Facts
Mean while a Contempt petition was filed by the said four MLAs in this court against the Speaker.	Facts
They complained that his action in preventing them from entering into the Assembly premises and from acting as members of the Assembly was in violation of the orders of this court dated September 6, 1991.	Facts
On October 3, 1991, this court passed another order affirming that all authorities of the State including the Governor must ensure that the orders of this Court dated September 6, 1991 are implemented.	Facts
Accordingly, the said four independent MLAs were issued invitation to attend the session on October 8, 1991.	Facts
The agenda relating to the business of the House showed two items for consideration on that day (1) a motion of confidence in the government and (2) a motion of no. confidence in the Speaker.	Facts
On October 8, 1991, 56 M LAs apart from the Speaker attended the session.	Facts
The four MLAs who were disqualified by the Speaker but who had obtained orders from this Court also attended but not Sri Ch.	Facts
Marak who did not obtain any orders from any court.	Facts
After the motion of confidence in the government was put to vote, the Speaker declared that 26 voted for the motion and 26 against.	Facts
In counting the votes casts in favour of the motion, he excluded the votes of the said four independent MLAs again.	Facts
Holding that there was a tie, he cast his vote against the motion and declared the motion lost.	Facts
He then adjourned the House sine die, evidently with a view to ward off the passing of motion against himself.	Facts
The thirty MLAs (including the said four independent MLAs) however, continued to stay in the House.	Facts
They elected a Speaker from among themselves and continued the business of the Assembly.	Facts
The new Speaker found on a scrutiny of the records relating to voting on the motion of confidence that actually 30 members have signed in favour of the motion and 26 against.	Facts
Accordingly, he declared that the motion of confidence in the government was carried.	Facts
They also passed the motion of no. confidence in the Speaker, Sri Kyndiah.	Facts
The 26 members who had voted against the motion had, of course, left the House by that time.	Facts
The said 30 MLAs thereafter sent a letter to the Governor affirming that they had voted in favour of the government and also in favour of the motion of no. confidence in the Speaker.	Facts
In spite of all this, the Chief Minister received a letter dated, October 9, 1991 from the Governor advising him to resign in view of the proceedings of the Assembly dated October 8, 1991.	Facts
The Governor observed in his letter that the dispute about the Speaker not taking cognizance of the orders of the Supreme Court was a matter between the Speaker and the Supreme Court and in that view of the matter, the Chief Minister should resign.	Facts
Immediately, thereupon, the Chief Minister apprised his advocate in the Supreme Court of the said letter of the Governor.	Facts
The counsel brought the matter to the notice of this Court and at 4.00 p.m. on the same day (October 9, 1991), this court passed the following order Since the matter is extremely urgent, we deem it fit to pass this further order asking the Governor while taking any decision on the question whether the Government has lost the motion of confidence and lost its majority in the House, to take into account, the two earlier orders dated 691991 and 3101991 of this Court and also to take into account how the aforesaid four appellants had cast their vote.	Facts
No. heed was paid to this order and on October 11, 1991, the President of India issued a proclamation under Article 356 of the Constitution declaring that he was satisfied on the basis of a report from the Governor of Meghalaya and other information received by him that a situation has arisen in which the.	Facts
Government of the State cannot be carried on in accordance with the provisions of the Constitution.	Facts
He accordingly dismissed the government and dissolved the Assembly.	Facts
Before proceeding further, it may be mentioned that by an order dated October 12, 1991, a Constitution Bench of this Court set aside the order of the Speaker dated August 17, 1989.	Facts
Both Houses of Parliament duly met and approved the proclamation.	Facts
It is a matter of deep regret that the Governor of Meghalaya did not think it his constitutional duty to give effect to the orders of this Court, not even after a specific direction to that effect.	None
He could not have been unaware of the obligation created by Article 144, viz., the duty of all authorities, civil and judicial, in the territory of India to act in aid of the Supreme Court and its orders.	None
By order dated October 9, 1991, he was specifically requested to take into account the orders of this Court while deciding whether the government has lost the confidence of the House and yet he ignored the same and reported to the President that the Ministry has lost the confidence of the House.	None
We are intrigued by the strange logic of the Governor that obedience to the orders of this Court relating to the disqualification of members of the House is a matter between the Speaker and the Supreme Court.	None
Evidently, he invoked this strange logic to enable him to say  as he wanted to say or as he was asked to say, as the case may be  that the Speakers decision that the Ministry has lost the confidence of the House, is valid and effective  at any rate, so far as he is concerned.	None
The Governor ought to have noted that this court had stayed the operation of the orders of the Speaker disqualifying the four independent members, which meant that the said four MLAs were entitled to participate in the proceedings of the Assembly and to vote.	None
They did vote in favour of the motion expressing confidence in the government.	None
The Speaker was, however, bent upon unseating the government by means fair or foul and with that view was openly flouting the orders of this Court.	None
He managed to declare that the government has lost the confidence of the House by excluding the votes of the said four members in clear violation of the orders of this Court.	None
It is surprising that the Governor chose to turn Nelsons eye upon the misdeeds of the Speaker and also chose to refuse to take note of the proceedings of the majority of members taken under the Speakership of another member elected by them.	None
It is equally curious that the Governor chose to report that a situation has arisen where the government of the State cannot be carried on in accordance with the provisions of the Constitution.	None
The violation of the provisions of the constitution was by Sri Kyndiah and not by the Ministry in office and yet Article 356 was resorted to by the President to dismiss the government on the basis of such a report.	None
That even such an ex facie unconstitutional proclamation was approved by both Houses of Parliament shows up the inadequacy of the safeguard envisaged in clause (3)  by which provision much store was laid by the counsel appearing for the Union of India as well as those supporting the impugned proclamations.	None
In this case too, the proclamation recites that the requisite satisfaction was arrived at on the basis of the report of the Governor and the other information received by the President but no.	None
such information or material has been brought to our notice.	None
We must conclude that there was none and that the recital to that effect is a mere mechanical one.	None
We must say in fairness to Sri Parasaran, learned counsel appearing for the Union of India that he did not seek to defend the proclamation in this case.	None
Accordingly, we hold the proclamation as unconstitutional.	Decision
But for the fact that since the date of proclamation, fresh elections have been held to the Assembly and a new House has come into existence, we would have certainly issued the writ and directed the restoration of the Lyngdoh ministry to office and restored the Assembly as well.	Decision
NAGALAND Elections to the Nagaland Assembly were held in November, 1987.	Facts
The strength of the Assembly was 60.	Facts
The position emerging from the election was Congress(l)35, Naga National Democratic Party 13 and Independents7.	Facts
The Congress (1) party formed the government with Sri Hokishe Sema as the Chief Minister.	Facts
In August, 1988, a split occurred in the ruling party whose strength was 34 at that time, one member having died.	Facts
The particulars of the split in the party are the following On July 28, 1988, 13 of the 34 MLAs informed the Speaker of the assembly that they have dissociated from the ruling party and have formed a separate party called Congress Ruling Party They requested the Speaker for allotment of separate seats for them in the Assembly, the session of which was to commence on August 28, 1988.	Facts
On July 30, 1988 the Speaker held that a split had occurred within the meaning of the Xth schedule of the Constitution in the ruling party.	Facts
Shri Vamuzo was one among the said 13 MLAs.	Facts
He informed the Governor on July 31, 1988 that he has secured the support of 35 of the 59 members of the Assembly and was in a position to form the ministry in the State.	Facts
At this stage, the Chief Secretary to the Government of Nagaland wrote to Shri Vamuzo on August 3, 1988 that according to the information received by him, the group of 13 MLAs aforesaid were wrongfully confined by him.	Facts
Shri Vamuzo denied the same and invited the Chief Secretary to come and verify the truth of the allegation from the said members themselves.	Facts
The members stated before the Chief Secretary that they were free agents and were not confined by any one.	Facts
On August 6, 1988 the Governor of Nagaland sent a report to the President of India about the formation of Congress Ruling Party.	Facts
He reported that in the past 25 years, eleven governments have been formed and that thirteen MLAs who had dissociated themselves from the Congress (1) party were allured with money.	Facts
He characterised the said weaning away of the thirteen members as incredible lack of political morality and complete disregard to the wishes of the electorate on the part of the breakaway congressmen.	Facts
He also stated that the said thirteen persons were kept in forcible confinement by Sri Vamuzo and another person and that the story of split in the party is not true.	Facts
He characterised the recognition accorded to the said group of thirteen members by the Speaker as hasty.	Facts
He also spoke of political horsetrading and machinations.	Facts
He referred to the insurgency in Nagaland and that indeed some of the members of the Assembly were having contacts with the insurgent groups.	Facts
He reported that the stability of the State may suffer due to the said episode and further that if the present affairs are allowed to continue, a serious development may ensue.	Facts
The Chief Minister, Sri Hokishe Sema, probably finding that he has lost the majority support in the House, submitted his resignation to the Governor and recommended the imposition of the Presidents rule.	Facts
On August 7, 1988, the President issued the proclamation under Article 356 assuming the functions of the government of the State of Nagaland.	Facts
The government was dismissed and the Assembly dissolved.	Facts
The action was challenged by Sri Vamuzo by way of a writ petition in the Guwahati High Court being C. R. No. 1414 of 1988.	Facts
The writ petition was heard by a Division Bench comprising the Chief Justice and Hansaria, J. Both the learned Judges agreed that the validity of the proclamation can be examined by the court and that the proclamation under Article 356 is not immune from judicial scrutiny.	Facts
But on the question of the effect and operation of Article 74(2), they differed.	Facts
The learned Chief Justice held the Union cannot be compelled to tender any information to this court covered by Article 74 of the Constitution relevant to the dissolution of the Nagaland assembly.	Facts
I am also of the view that the Union of India can legally claim all documents relevant to the dissolution of the Nagaland assembly as privileged documents and a class documents under Section 123 of the Evidence Act.	None
Therefore, the objection that the courts do not have powers to call for the information from the President of India in view of Article 74(2) of the Constitution is sustained.	None
Since the Nagaland legislative assembly is dissolved by the two Houses of Parliament, no. relief can be granted in the circumstances of this case.	None
Accordingly, he proposed to dismiss the writ petition.	None
Hansaria, J., however, took a contrary view.	None
The learned Judge held that the material which formed part of other information but has not been produced before the court, does not form part of the advice tendered by the council of ministers to the President.	None
The court is, therefore, entitled to see the said material and for that purpose the Union of India must be given ten days time for producing the same.	None
If, however, they decline to do so, the court would have no. alternative but to act upon the present material and the Union of India will have to take the consequences of such a course.	None
The learned Judge did not propose to dispose of the writ petition but to wait for ten days and then pronounce the final orders.	None
In view of the said difference of opinion, the matter was referred to a third Judge, but before the third Judge could hear the matter, the Union of India moved this Court for grant of Special Leave.	Facts
Special Leave was granted and the proceedings in the High Court stayed.	None
We have discussed the effect and scope of Article 74(2) elsewhere.	None
In the light of the same, the view taken by Hansaria, J. (as he then was) must be held to be the correct one and not the view taken by the learned Chief Justice.	None
This Special Leave Petition is accordingly disposed of with the above direction.	Decision
Inasmuch as fresh elections have since been held, the High Court may consider the advisability of proceeding with the matter at this point of time.	Decision
MADHYA PRADESH, RAJASTHAN AND HIMACHAL PRADESH In the elections held in February, 1990, the BJP emerged as the Majority party in the Assemblies of Uttar Pradesh, Madhya Pradesh, Rajasthan and Himachal Pradesh and formed the government therein.	Facts
On December 6, 1992, the Ram JanmabhoomiBabri Masjid structure (disputed structure) was demolished by the kar sevaks who had gathered there in response to appeals by the BJP, VHP, Bajrang Dal, Shiv Sena and some other organisations.	Facts
Following the demolition at Ayodhya on 6th December, 1992, the Government of Uttar Pradesh resigned.	Facts
It was dismissed by the President and the Legislative Assembly dissolved by a proclamation under Article 356 issued on the same day.	Facts
The proclamation does not refer either to the report of the Governor nor does it say that the President had received any information otherwise.	Facts
Be that as it may, the validity of the said proclamation not being in issue before us, we need not express any opinion in that behalf.	Facts
The demolition of the disputed mosque had serious repercussions all over the country as also in some neighbouring countries.	Facts
A number of temples were reportedly demolished there.	Facts
Serious disturbance to law and order occurred in various parts of the country resulting in considerable loss of lives and property.	Facts
By an order dated December 10, 1992 issued under Section (1) of the Unlawful Activities (Prevention) Act, 1967 (37 of 1967), the Government of India banned several alleged communal organisations including RSS, VHP and Bajrang Dal.	Facts
MADHYA PRADESH On December 8, 1992, the Governor of Madhya Pradesh sent a report to the President setting out the fast deteriorating law and order situation in the State in the wake of widespread acts of violence, arson and looting.	Facts
He observed in his report that the lack of faith in the ability of the State Government to stem the tide primarily because of the political leaderships overt and covert support to the associate communal organisations seem to point out that there is breakdown of the administrative machinery of the State.	Facts
He followed it up with another report on December 10, 1992 wherein he mentioned about the violence spreading to hither to peaceful areas.	None
On December 13, 1992, he sent his third report enclosing the photocopy of a letter received from the Executive Director, Bharat Heavy Electricals Limited (BHEL), Bhopal dated December .11, 1992.	Facts
The said letter, said the Governor, indicated the abject failure of the law and order machinery to provide safety and security to life and property in the areas in and around BHEL factory.	Facts
The letter also spoke of the pressure brought on the administration to accommodate the so called kar sewaks in BHEL area .	Facts
The Governor termed them as extremely serious developments that deserve a high level probe.	Facts
The third report further stated that with the reported statement of the Chief Minister Sri Sunder Lal Patwa that the decision of banning the RSS and VHP was unfortunate, the State Governments credibility to sincerely implement the Centres direction in the matter is under a cloudthere is a question mark as to how BJP leaders like Sri Patwa who swore by the values and traditions of the RSS will be able to implement the ban both in letter and spirit.	Facts
The VHPs decision to observe December 13 as Black Day all over the country to protest against the above mentioned ban and its decision to observe protest week against these heinous laws from December 14 to 20 are moves fraught with danger, particularly in the present context.	Facts
The Governor recommended that considering this and looked in the background of the RSS etc., contemplating on a fresh strategy to chalk out its future plan and the possibility of the leaders of the banned organisations going underground taking advantage of the soft reaction of the administration have reasons to be convinced that there should not be any further delay in imposition of Presidents rule according to Article 356 of the Constitution of India.	Facts
HIMACHAL PRADESH The Governor of Himachal Pradesh sent a report on December 15, 1992 wherein he stated inter alia there is no. dispute on the point that the Chief Minister and his cabinet had instigated the kar sevaks from Himachal Pradesh to participate in the kar seva on the 6th December, 1992.	Facts
Some of the Ministers expressed their desire even openly, provided the party High command permitted to do so.	Facts
Consequently, a large number of kar sevaks including some BJP MLAs participated in the kar seva from Himachal Pradesh.	Facts
A Member of the Vidhan Sabha publicly admitted that he had participated in the demolition of the Babri Masjid (Indian Express dated 15121992, Chandigarh Edition).	Facts
Though Sri Shanta Kumar met me on December 13, 1992 and had informed me that he desired to implement the ban orders imposed by the Government of India on RSS, VHP and three other organisations and that he has already issued directions in this regard but since the Chief Minister himself is a member of RSS, therefore, he is not in a position to implement these directions honestly and effectively.	Facts
Most of the people of the State also feel alikeAs a matter of fact, when the Chief Minister him self and some of the colleagues are members of the banned RSS, then it is not possible for the administrative machinery to implement the ban honestly, especially when some of the Ministers are openly criticising the ban on these communal organisations.	Facts
He, therefore, recommended imposition of the Presidents rule.	Facts
RAJASTHAN	None
The report of the Governor of Rajasthan, recommending imposition of the Presidents rule, stated the folowing facts the government of Rajasthan has played an obvious role in the Ayodhya episode.	Facts
The BJP has control over RSS, VHP and Bajrang Dal which are now banned by the Centre.	Facts
The said ban is not being implemented at all.	Facts
Indeed, one of the Ministers had resigned and along with 22 MLAs and 15, 500 BJP workers had participated in the kar seva at Ayodhya on December 12, 1992.	Facts
They were given a royal send off and when they returned, they were given a similar royal welcome by the influential people in the political set up running the government.	Facts
The law and order has been very bad for more than a week, the dominant character being the antiminority on whom largely atrocities have been committed.	Facts
The administration could not function effectively under the present political set up.	Facts
He expressed the apprehension that it would be extremely difficult to expect the administration to function objectively, effectively and in accordance with the rule of law and that a situation has arisen in which the government of the State cannot be carried on in accordance with the provisions of the Constitution.	Facts
On December 15, 1992, the President issued three proclamations dismissing all the three governments in Madhya Pradesh, Rajasthan and Himachal Pradesh and dissolving their Legislative Assemblies.	Facts
The action was purported to be taken on the basis of the reports of the Governors concerned as well as on the basis of other information received.	Facts
The validity of the proclamations was challenged immediately by filing writ petitions in the appropriate High Courts.	Facts
The Madhya Pradesh High Court allowed the same which is challenged by the Union of India in Civil Appeal Nos. 1692, 1692A1692C of 1993.	Facts
The writ petitions relating to Rajasthan and Himachal Pradesh were withdrawn to this Court and are numbered as Transferred Case No. 9 of 1993 and Transferred Case No. 8 of 1993 respectively.	Facts
The petitioners challenged the proclamation as mala fide, vitiated by extraneous considerations and an instance of political vendetta.	Facts
It is submitted that incidents of disturbance to law and order cannot attract action under Article 356.	Facts
In any event, in Himachal Pradesh, there was not a single instance.	Facts
All the three governments were faithfully implementing all the Central and State laws.	Facts
The impugned proclamations, it is submitted, are the result of internal differences among the leaders of the Congress party and are not supportable in law.	Facts
It is submitted by the learned counsel for the petitioners that the imposition of the Presidents rule in the States of Madhya Pradesh, Rajasthan and Himachal Pradesh was mala fide, based on no. satisfaction and was purely a political act.	Arguments of Petitioner
Mere fact that communal disturbance and or instances of arson and looting took place is no. ground for imposing the Presidents rule.	Arguments of Petitioner
Indeed, such incidents took place in several Congress(I) ruled States as well  in particular, in the State of Maharashtra  on a much larger scale and yet no.	Arguments of Petitioner
action was taken to displace those governments whereas action was taken only against BJP governments.	Arguments of Petitioner
It is pointed out that so far as Himachal Pradesh is concerned, there were no. communal disturbances at all.	Arguments of Petitioner
There was no. law and order problem worth the name.	Arguments of Petitioner
Even the Governors report did not speak of any such incidents.	Arguments of Petitioner
The governments of Madhya Pradesh, Rajasthan and Himachal Pradesh, it is argued, cannot be held responsible for what happened at Ayodhya on December 6, 1992.	Arguments of Petitioner
For that incident, the Government of Uttar Pradesh had resigned owning responsibility therefor and it was dismissed.	Arguments of Petitioner
That is not under challenge.	Arguments of Petitioner
But the Governments of these three States were in no. way connected with the said incident and could not have been dismissed on account of the said incident.	Arguments of Petitioner
It is also pointed out that according to the report of the Governor of Himachal Pradesh, the Chief Minister met him and indicated clearly that he was desirous of and was implementing the ban and that some arrests were also made.	Arguments of Petitioner
In such a situation, there was no. reason for the Governor to believe, or to report, that the Chief Minister is not sincere or keen to implement the ban on the said organisations.	Arguments of Petitioner
As a matter of fact, the Tribunal under Unlawful Activities (Prevention) Act, 1967, has declared the ban on R.S.S. as illegal and accordingly the ban has since been revoked.	Arguments of Petitioner
The nonimplementation of an illegal ban cannot be made the basis of action under Article 356.	Arguments of Petitioner
Assuming that there was such an inaction or refusal, it cannot be made a ground for dismissing the State Government and for dissolving the Assembly.	Arguments of Petitioner
The Union Government has also not disclosed what other material information they had received on the basis of which the President had acted, though a recital to that effect has been made in the proclamations.	Arguments of Petitioner
The action taken by the President cannot be justified by producing the material gathered later.	Arguments of Petitioner
The respondents must disclose the information that was before the President when he issued the impugned proclamations.	Arguments of Petitioner
The White Paper now placed before the Court was not in existence on December 15, 1992.	Arguments of Petitioner
The manifestos issued by the B.J. P. from time to time cannot constitute the information referred to in the proclamation  not, in any event, legally relevant material.	Arguments of Petitioner
The counter filed by the Union of India in Madhya Pradesh High Court in M. P. No. 237/93 (Sunderlal Patwa v. Union of India) does not refer to or disclose the other information received by the President.	Arguments of Petitioner
Even in the counters filed in writ petitions questioning the proclamations relating to Himachal Pradesh and Rajasthan, no.	Arguments of Petitioner
such material is disclosed.	Arguments of Petitioner
It was the duty of the Union Government to have disclosed to the Court the material information upon which the requisite satisfaction was formed, more so because the proclamations themselves do not refer to any such material.	Arguments of Petitioner
Since they have failed to do so, an adverse inference should be drawn against them.	Arguments of Petitioner
Article 74(2), it is argued, does not and cannot relieve the Union of India of this obligation.	Arguments of Petitioner
The power and remedy of judicial review, it is argued, cannot be rendered ineffective with reference to Art. 74(2).	Arguments of Petitioner
A counter affidavit was filed by the Union of India in the writ petition filed in the Madhya Pradesh High Court questioning the Proclamation with respect to that State.	Arguments of Respondent
Apart from the legal contentions, the following facts are stated therein The reports of the Governor disclosed that the State Government had miserably failed to protect the citizens and property of the State against internal disturbance.	Arguments of Respondent
On the basis of the said reports, the President formed the requisite satisfaction.	Arguments of Respondent
The circumstances in the State of M.P. were different from several other States where too serious disturbance to law and order took place.	Arguments of Respondent
There is no. comparison between both situations.	Arguments of Respondent
Besides Bhopal, overall situation in the State of M.P. was such that there was sufficient and cogent reasons to be satisfied that the Government in the State could not be carried on in accordance with the provisions of the Constitution.	Arguments of Respondent
It is denied that there was no. law and order situation in the State.	Arguments of Respondent
The Governors reports are based upon relevant material and are made bona fide and after due verification.	None
354.	Arguments of Respondent
The allegations made against Sri Arjun Singh, Minister for Human Resource Development are baseless.	Arguments of Respondent
The decision was a collective decision of the Council of Ministers.	Arguments of Respondent
No. comparison with regard to the state of affairs in the State of Madhya Pradesh can be made with those of other States.	Arguments of Respondent

In the counter affidavit filed in the writ petition (Transferred Case No. 8 of 1993) relating to Himachal Pradesh, the very same objection as are put forward in the counter affidavit filed in the Madhya Pradesh case have been reiterated.	Arguments of Respondent
In the parawise replies, it is stated that the events of 6th December, 1992 were not the handiwork of few persons but that the public attitude and statements of various groups and political parties including B.J.P. led to the destruction of the structure in question and caused great damage to the very secular fabric of the country and created communal discord and disharmony all over the country including Himachal Pradesh.	Arguments of Respondent
It is stated that the repercussions of the event cannot be judged by comparing the number of persons killed in different States.	None

356.	Arguments of Respondent

None
It is also stated that, according to the definite information available to the Government of India, members of the R.S.S. were not only present on the spot at Ayodhya but actually participated in the demolition and that they were responsible for promotion of communal disharmony.	Arguments of Respondent
It is for this reason that it was banned.	Arguments of Respondent

The situation in each State has to be assessed differently.	Arguments of Respondent
The averment of the petitioner that the State Government implemented the ban on R.S.S. properly is denied.	Arguments of Respondent

It can also be addressed to the Prime Minister.	Arguments of Respondent
Besides the report of the Governor, other information was also available on which the President had formed his satisfaction.	Arguments of Respondent
The correctness, adequacy or sufficiency of the material contained in the Governors report is not justiciable and cannot be gone into by the Court.	Arguments of Respondent
The allegations of mala fide, capricious and arbitrary exercise of power are denied.	Arguments of Respondent
No. irrelevant material was taken into consideration by the President and hence, it is averred, the satisfaction of the President is not judicially reviewable.	Arguments of Respondent
357.	Arguments of Respondent
The learned counsel for Union of India and other counsel supporting the impugned proclamations put their case thus the main plank and the primary programme of B.J.P. was the construction of a Ram temple at the very site where the Babri Masjid stood.	Arguments of Respondent
The party openly proclaimed that they will removerelocate, as they called it  the Babri Masjid structure since according to them the Babri Masjid was superimposed on an existing Ram temple by Emperor Babar.	Arguments of Respondent
The party came to power in all the four States on the said plank and since then had been working towards the said goal.	Arguments of Respondent
It is the one single goal of all the leaders of B.J.P., their Ministers, Legislators and all cadres.	Arguments of Respondent
For this purpose, they have been repeatedly gathering kar sevaks from all corners at Ayodhya from time to time.	Arguments of Respondent
In the days immediately preceding December 6, 1992, their leaders have been inciting and exhorting their followers to demolish the Babri Masjid and to build a temple there.	Arguments of Respondent
The Ministers in Madhya Pradesh, Himachal Pradesh and Rajasthan took active part in organising and despatching kar sevaks to Ayodhya.	Arguments of Respondent
When the kar sevaks returned from Ayodhya after demolishing the Masjid, they were welcomed as heroes by those very persons.	Arguments of Respondent
Many of the Ministers and Chief Ministers were members of R.S.S. and were protesting against the ban on it.	Arguments of Respondent
They could not, therefore, be trusted to enforce the ban, notwithstanding the protestations to the contrary by some of them.	Arguments of Respondent
358.	Arguments of Respondent
The manifesto issued by the BJP on the eve of May June, 1991 midterm poll States that the B.J. P. seeks the restoration of Ram Janmabhoomi in Ayodhya only by way of a symbolic righting of historic wrongs, so that the old unhappy chapter of acrimony could be ended, and a Grand National Reconciliation effected.	None
At another place under the head Sri Ram Mandir at Janmasthan, the following statement occurrs BJP firmly believes that construction of Ram Mandir at Janmasthan is a symbol of the vindication of our cultural heritage and national selfrespect.	Reasoning
For BJP it is purely a national issue and it will not allow any vested interests to give it a sectarian and communal colour.	Arguments of Respondent
Hence, the party is committed to build.	Arguments of Respondent
Shri Ram Mandir at Janmasthan by relocating superimposed Babri structure with due respect.	None
Standing by themselves, it is true, the above statements may not mean that the programme envisaged unlawful or forcible demolition of the disputed structure.	Arguments of Respondent
The said statement are also capable of being understood as meaning that the party proposed to vindicate their stand in Courts that the disputed structure was in fact the Ram Janmasthan which was forcibly converted into a mosque by Emperor Babar and that only thereafter they will relocate the said structure and build Ram temple at that site.	Arguments of Respondent
But, says the counsel, if we read the above statements in the light of the speeches and acts of the leaders of the B.J.P., referred to in the White Paper issued by the Government of India, there would hardly be any room for such beneficial interpretation.	Arguments of Respondent

The counsel for the respondents argued further that what happened on December 6, 1992 did not happen in a day.	None

They had been actively campaigning for the construction of Ram temple at the disputed site.	None
They had been speaking of relocating the disputed structure which only meant that they wanted the disputed structure removed and a Ram temple constructed in that very place.	None

On the contrary, the following statement occurs under the heading Ayodhya Ayodhya In their actions and utterances, the forces of pseudosecularism convey the unmistakable impression of a deep repugnance for all things Hindu.	None
Indeed, in their minds Hindu has come to be associated with communal.	Arguments of Respondent

For them Sahmat is secular and Saffron communal.	Arguments of Respondent
Although the facts of the dispute are well known, certain features merit repetition.	Arguments of Respondent
First, it was always apparent that a vast majority of Hindus were totally committed to the construction of a grand temple for Lord Rama at the site where puja has been performed uninterruptedly since 1948 and where besides, no. namaz has been offered since 1936.	Arguments of Respondent
The structure built by the Moghul Emperor Babar was viewed by the Hindus as a symbol of national humiliation.	None
Second, the election of 1991 in Uttar Pradesh centred on the Ayodhya dispute.	None
It was a vitual referendum on Ram Janmabhoomi and the BJP with its promise to facilitate the construction of the Ram Temple won the election.	Arguments of Respondent
However, this mandate did not prevent the Congress and other pseudosecular parties from wilfully obstructing the initiatives of the Uttar Pradesh government.	Arguments of Respondent
Everything, from administrative subterfuge to judicial delay, was used by the opponents of the temple to prevent the BJP government from fulfilling its promise to the electorate.	None
On December 6, 1992 kar sevaks from all over India assembled in Ayodhya to begin the reconstruction of the Rama Temple at the site adjoining the garbha griha.	None
Matters took an unexpected turn when, angered by the obstructive tactics of the Narasimha Rao government, inordinate judicial delays and pseudosecularist taunts, the kar sevaks took matters into their own hands, demolished the disputed structure and constructed a makeshift temple for Lord Rama at the garbha griha.	Arguments of Respondent
Owing responsibility for its inability to prevent the demolition, the BJPgovernment headed by Shri Kalyan Singh submitted its resignation.	None
A disoriented Central government was not content with the imposition of Presidents rule in Uttar Pradesh.	Arguments of Respondent
In violation of democratic norms, the centre dismissed the BJP governments in Rajasthan, Madhya Pradesh and Himachal Pradesh.	Arguments of Respondent
Further, it banned the Rashtriya Swayamsevak Sangh, Vishwa Hindu Parishad and Bajrang Dal.	Arguments of Respondent
Worst of all, in collusion with other rootless forces the government unleashed a vicious propaganda offensive aimed at belittling the Hindus.	None
The kar sevaks were denigrated as fascists, lumpens and vandals, and December 6, was described as a national shame .	Arguments of Respondent
Recently, the CBI has filed chargesheets against leaders of the BJP and the Vishwa Hind Parishad with the purpose of projecting them as criminals.	Arguments of Respondent
This relentless onslaught of the pseudosecular forces against the people of India had very serious consequences.	None
For a start, it created a wide emotional gulf between the rulers and the people.	Arguments of Respondent

The counsel further pointed out the significance of the total inaction on the part of the top leaders of the B.J.P. present near the disputed structure at Ayodhya on December 6, 1992.	Arguments of Respondent
They took no. steps whatsoever to stop the demolition.	Arguments of Respondent

It is stated in the report of the Himachal Pradesh Governor that the Chief Minister himself was a member of the RSS.	Arguments of Respondent
In the report of the Governor of Madhya Pradesh also, it is stated that the Chief Minister and other ministers swore by the values and traditions of the RSS.	Arguments of Respondent

Thus, a common thread runs through all the four B.J.P. governments and binds them together, say the counsel.	Arguments of Respondent

The demolition of the disputed structure was no.	Arguments of Respondent
ordinary event.	Arguments of Respondent

It had adverse international repercussions as well.	Arguments of Respondent
A number of Hindu temples were demolished in Pakistan and Bangladesh in reprisal of the demolition at Ayodhya.	Arguments of Respondent

They had to go.	None
The learned counsel for the respondents submitted further that the R.S.S. was banned on December 10, 1992.	Arguments of Respondent

In such circumstances, the respective Governors were of the opinion that the said Chief Ministers cannot be expected to, or relied upon to, implement the ban sincerely.	Arguments of Respondent
It cannot be said to be an unreasonable or unfounded opinion.	Arguments of Respondent

ordinary event.	Arguments of Respondent

Arguments of Respondent

Arguments of Respondent
